    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer12131805075702712935"><b>LET THE GAMES BEGIN....</b><br/><br/>Quillan is a territory on the verge of destruction. The people have lost control of their own future and must struggle simply to survive. The only chance they have of finding a better life is by playing the Quillan Games. Hosted by a strange pair of game masters, Veego and LaBerge, the games are a mix of sport and combat. They use the people of Quill</span>
  <span id="freeText12131805075702712935" style="display:none"><b>LET THE GAMES BEGIN....</b><br /><br />Quillan is a territory on the verge of destruction. The people have lost control of their own future and must struggle simply to survive. The only chance they have of finding a better life is by playing the Quillan Games. Hosted by a strange pair of game masters, Veego and LaBerge, the games are a mix of sport and combat. They use the people of Quillan as pawns for their amusement as they force them to enter competitions that range from physical battles, to impossible obstacle courses, to computer-driven tests of agility. To triumph in the games is to live the life of a king. To lose is to die.<br /><br />This is the dangerous and deadly situation that Bobby Pendragon finds on Quillan. He quickly realizes that the only way to save this troubled territory is to beat Veego and LaBerge at their own games and dismantle their horrible fun house. But there is more at stake for Bobby. The prize for winning the Quillan Games may be discovering the truth of what it really means to be a Traveler.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12131805075702712935" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

And, as Marta stated, this book came out two years before the Hunger Games was first released.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5093309868692589396"><b>Complete 5 Golden Stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1599332896ra/30067473.gif' width='' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>BOOM! Surprise!<br/><br/>MacHale surly is the man of the last moments...<br/>& this book Probably contains one big Turning Point, the Second Climax that push the story more to the edge, the Beginning of the End (or whatever you call it) of the whole saga.<br/><br/><br/>Quillan is not one of my favourite territories, but "the Quillan Games" is one of my favourites in this epic journey through time & space!<br/>Fabulous! Fantastic!<br/>we are near the end & things getting serious & dark & more complicated! *Joker'</span>
  <span id="freeText5093309868692589396" style="display:none"><b>Complete 5 Golden Stars</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1599332896ra/30067473.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>BOOM! Surprise!<br><br>MacHale surly is the man of the last moments...<br>&amp; this book Probably contains one big Turning Point, the Second Climax that push the story more to the edge, the Beginning of the End (or whatever you call it) of the whole saga.<br><br><br>Quillan is not one of my favourite territories, but "the Quillan Games" is one of my favourites in this epic journey through time &amp; space!<br>Fabulous! Fantastic!<br>we are near the end &amp; things getting serious &amp; dark &amp; more complicated! *Joker's mad laughter*<br><br><br><b>Let the Games Begin....</b><br><br>in this territory,<br><i>You Play &amp; You Pay...</i><br><br>First of all, if you are comparing this book to "the Hunger Games", I must tell you a few things:<br><br>1) this book originally published almost 3 years before the Hunger Games, in 2006.<br>2) Yeah, this territory is a future society under a choking pressure of its ruler, but it's another level in Pendragon's journey through time &amp; space. Its whole plot is totally different &amp; complicated which categorized as sci-fi. (though Now I'm thinking this book is my first encounter with a Dystopian world.)<br>3) this book is a lot funnier &amp; lighter (which doesn't reduce the criticality of the main story) than that series (&amp; LESS brutal &amp; disturbing)<br><br>thank you<br><br>We shall continue:<br><br>to uncover the mystery behind the scene, to find Saint Dane, discover &amp; neutralize his plans for this territory, Pendragon should beat the masters of these Dangerous Games in their Mad Fun house!<br><br>Lots of FUN! (You can't rule that out with Bobby on the stage, even in this seriousness.)<br>Lots of Games!<br>Lots of Riddles!<br>Lots of Craziness!<br>Lots of Mysteries!<br><br>in this Gray world of Games &amp; Gambles<br>so much Fun,<br>yet,<br>so much tension<br><br>&amp; be careful of the Feelz attack!<br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1599581877ra/30079088.gif" width="" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br>but don't forget the Sweet Fourteen!<br><br><br>That beautiful Ending &amp; That shocking, exciting, dangerous, thrilling, emotional Ending (two kinds of ending, because if you’re familiar with these books, you know it usually has 2.)<br>MacHale totally knows how to throw something captivating.<br>I'm just glad I had the opportunity to know his works &amp; his world.<br><br>I know it's crazy, but I just want to read it again!</span>

The book takes place after The Rivers of Zadaa and was released on May 16, 2006 in Canada and the US. The story takes place on a territory called Quillan, in the city of Rune, whose population live dreary lives under the rule of the megacorporation 'Blok'. Many people gamble on the eponymous games in hope of a better life; but may lose their lives, their families, or their professions if the bet fails.           <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4617391-lauren?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4617391-lauren?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2224772583" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10220976887948896708">I mean... wow. Once I started really reading, I flew through this book. I read 200+ pages in my last sitting alone and man, what a read. This book was so intense from start to finish, I can honestly say whenever I was reading I was on the edge of my seat.<br/><br/>So much happened in this book, but on the flip side, so much was introduced and shit was blown open left and right leaving me with way more questions than I could ever have answers for.<br/><br/>The last little bit of Bobby's journal definitely gave me so</span>
  <span id="freeText10220976887948896708" style="display:none">I mean... wow. Once I started really reading, I flew through this book. I read 200+ pages in my last sitting alone and man, what a read. This book was so intense from start to finish, I can honestly say whenever I was reading I was on the edge of my seat.<br /><br />So much happened in this book, but on the flip side, so much was introduced and shit was blown open left and right leaving me with way more questions than I could ever have answers for.<br /><br />The last little bit of Bobby's journal definitely gave me some hope for the future, but everything Saint Dane talked to him about only left more questions. Aghhh<br /><br />This book reminded me a lot of a mix of The Hunger Games (which, in all honesty I think borrowed a lot from this book) but also a little with the competition from The Goblet of Fire in the whole last set of games. It's always interesting to see parallels between different books, it's always been something I enjoy.<br /><br />But, because it was similar to those two books, it goes without saying that there were deaths, and it wasn't a walk in the park. Not that any of Bobby's adventures are, but this one went above and beyond anything he'd had to do before.<br /><br />I knew there was something fishy about the games and where those two idiots came from, and I also called it with Green, but I won't get into too much of that. <br /><br />I'm so glad that Courtney is okay, but I'm livid with everything happening with Mark. I want answers and I cannot wait to pick up the next book to hopefully have some stuff explained.<br /><br />Yet again, I have to thank my boyfriend for introducing me to this series and prompting me to read it.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer74340132380640620">Like always, the Pendragon series is full of twists and turns and good and evil. Espeically this one.<br/>Book Seven; <u>The Quillan Games.</u><br/><br/>Bobby travels through the flume to the territory of Quillan. What he sees there is <i>not</i> pretty: A company larger than the goverment called BLOK is controling everything. Litterally; everything.<br/>BLOK creates thier own style and color of clothes, so people can only wear what BLOK gives them: black, dark green and grey. That's it. No more color.<br/>Why can the people of Quill</span>
  <span id="freeText74340132380640620" style="display:none">Like always, the Pendragon series is full of twists and turns and good and evil. Espeically this one.<br />Book Seven; <u>The Quillan Games.</u><br /><br />Bobby travels through the flume to the territory of Quillan. What he sees there is <i>not</i> pretty: A company larger than the goverment called BLOK is controling everything. Litterally; everything.<br />BLOK creates thier own style and color of clothes, so people can only wear what BLOK gives them: black, dark green and grey. That's it. No more color.<br />Why can the people of Quillan only wear what BLOK gives them? Becuase it is the <b>only</b> bussiness; others closed down because citizens came like hungry sheep to the low prieces of BLOK.<br />People became so incredibly poor becuase when the worked for BLOK, BLOK payed close to nothing. Bottom line is: the people of Quillan are zombies; they obey every little thing BLOK tells they do to beucase they are terrifed they might get killed in the Games if they disagree. The Games are turnometns BLOK made to earn money; deadly fights and obsticle courses, tests of wit and will.<br />Booby must somehow stop these Games that are destorying the territory and its people...but then, he gets tricked into competing in the Games, and is suddenly everyone's simbol of hope; he is a symbol to the people telling them not to give in to the way things are. <br />"Rise up and fight BLOK, the company the is destoring your lives! Get revenge!"<br />Can Bobby help the devistayed people of Quillan?<br /><br />I thought this book was wonderful, the author did a great job. And he occasonaly tosses in hilarious comments that make me laugh like crazy. A few paragraphsa were predictable, but all-in-all, it was a great book. His characters are memerable; good and evil, and he writes fight scense that stick in your head forever! And the ending was a pure cliffhanger! <br />I loved this book.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8332161790840567257">This is the first time I have lost sleep worrying about what will happen in a book. I should have just read the whole thing and stayed up the whole night! Yeesh!<br/><br/>But this book is just amazing. This whole series is amazing. Each book goes to a new territory that has a problem and each problem is something we can all relate to. This book actually got me terrified--because its situation reminds me of what might happen if a huge company like Wal-mart takes over everything. <br/><br/>And the characters in this </span>
  <span id="freeText8332161790840567257" style="display:none">This is the first time I have lost sleep worrying about what will happen in a book. I should have just read the whole thing and stayed up the whole night! Yeesh!<br /><br />But this book is just amazing. This whole series is amazing. Each book goes to a new territory that has a problem and each problem is something we can all relate to. This book actually got me terrified--because its situation reminds me of what might happen if a huge company like Wal-mart takes over everything. <br /><br />And the characters in this series are hugely complex and developed, and really seem like real people. There is no "one-faced" characters. And because of that it's even easier to relate to them and to be gripped by the story.<br /><br />There are so many things in this book that throw you off-balance. D.J. MacHale includes so many mind-blowing twists and turns you feel positively overwhelmed! I think it's this, the feeling like you are going through the same troubling feelings as Bobby does, that makes this series so popular. It's incredibly addicting, and it does not let you go. <br /><br />This book is one of the best in the series.<br /><br />And this series is the best. xD</span>

<div id="review_142729464" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/142729464" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4737882-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1295993551p2/4737882.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/142729464?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/4737882-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4737882-anne?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4737882-anne?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer142729464" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6144655704426338067">I started reading this series forever ago. Not even kidding. Remember those little leaflets of Scholastic books that you used to get in elementary school, which would prompt you to beg your parents for pocket money so you could order one? I'm pretty sure I bought the first 4 books out of one of those. Then stuff happened. Mostly, I bought other books instead. I read the next two from the library and then just didn't read the rest (I think this had something to do with the fact that I was reading</span>
  <span id="freeText6144655704426338067" style="display:none">I started reading this series forever ago. Not even kidding. Remember those little leaflets of Scholastic books that you used to get in elementary school, which would prompt you to beg your parents for pocket money so you could order one? I'm pretty sure I bought the first 4 books out of one of those. Then stuff happened. Mostly, I bought other books instead. I read the next two from the library and then just didn't read the rest (I think this had something to do with the fact that I was reading them as they came out and by the time the next one came out, I was thinking about other books). Anyways, I saw this, and the next one, in the library the other day like a blast from the past and I decided to pick them up. It took me a while to finish, mostly because I'm not as invested in the series as I once was, but I am now prepared to (finally) review it!<br /><br />This book, more than anything else, reminds me of The Hunger Games, though of course it was published many years earlier. Now before you rush out to buy it on that statement alone, let me remind you that this is the 7th book in a fairly long series, and you will probably be extremely lost if you start there (and the rest aren't even remotely Hunger Games ish. Sorry).<br /><br />The premise of the world (called "territory" in this series) Quillan is a world much like ours that has been taken over by a single company. This company controls everything, from what foods you eat to what television you watch. Similar to the Hunger Games, the main form of entertainment is the "games," most of which are deadly, and all of which are televised (on big screens in the street too, you can't possibly miss it). The people have forgotten their rich heritage and forgotten how to think. Our hero, Bobby Pendragon, is swept into the games and forced to fight for his life only minutes after arriving in the territory, without a clue what is going on.<br /><br />It is interesting, to me, to pick up a series that you never finished as a kid. I can see why I loved it - it is very original and I still love that. There are so many different territories that it seems like MacHale gets to world build constantly, but that doesn't detract from the action. He somehow has figured out how to build his worlds in a way that is quick but gives a full sense of where you are.<br /><br />Then, of course, there are the sections about Bobby's two friends Courtney and Mark, who still live in our world (Second Earth in the series). They are his acolytes, and we see Bobby's entire story through their eyes - he magically sends them journals that they have to read and keep safe for him... I forget why, it's very early on in the series, and hasn't been that important yet.<br /><br />*SPOILER ALERT!*<br /><br />But the thing that made this book stand out from the rest of the series, for me, is how twisty it has become. I don't remember how long Bobby has been traveling on his own, but he is now making decisions for himself, trying to figure out who to trust. He makes some definite mistakes in this one. We don't find out until the very end, but someone Bobby trusts basically screws him over. This is the novel, much like Book 4 of Harry Potter, that marks a turning point in the series. Bobby is becoming an adult. It's a really important part of the series, and I like how MacHale deals with it. It happens so fast that when Courtney sees him at the end, she doesn't recognize him.<br /><br />Bottom line: If you liked Hunger Games and Harry Potter, this series is definitely for you. It'll be a little weird at first, but give it a chance and I can almost guarantee it'll grow on you.<br /><br />This series is 10 books long and was finished in 2009. The first novel is The Merchant of Death and can be found in both novel and graphic novel formats.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6144655704426338067" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2986579168" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2986579168" />
    <a title="Beth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4063913-beth"><img alt="Beth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351396026p2/4063913.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2986579168?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth" href="/user/show/4063913-beth">Beth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4063913-beth?shelf=project-nostalgia">project-nostalgia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4063913-beth?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2986579168" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3129446310773406607">This is the high point of the series. It’s <i>great.</i><br/><br/>It’s also the reason I started this reread in the first place - my memory of <i>The Hunger Games</i> being eerily similar to it - my memories of googling trying to find someone else who thought so (I was unsuccessful) - and that I remembered basically nothing else about it. <br/><br/>I found out a few things: this was a good series all along, and I see why my friends and I read it. Also, I don’t remember anything about <i>The Hunger Games</i>, which is a weird feeling. <br/><br/>S</span>
  <span id="freeText3129446310773406607" style="display:none">This is the high point of the series. It’s <i>great.</i><br /><br />It’s also the reason I started this reread in the first place - my memory of <i>The Hunger Games</i> being eerily similar to it - my memories of googling trying to find someone else who thought so (I was unsuccessful) - and that I remembered basically nothing else about it. <br /><br />I found out a few things: this was a good series all along, and I see why my friends and I read it. Also, I don’t remember anything about <i>The Hunger Games</i>, which is a weird feeling. <br /><br />So, <i>The Quillan Games.</i> It’s about Bobby ending up on a territory which is oppressed by a corporation controlling everyone’s lives, essentially forced into betting on a series of games which are broadcast throughout the territory. Bobby’s forced to be a challenger and play in the games, and he has a front row seat to the collapse of a territory. It’s good stuff. Bobby losing makes for a good story, and this is the book where the worldbuilding builds up to something really big, and it’s exciting and propulsive and compelling reading. <br /><br />I’m not going to reread <i>The Hunger Games</i> to see if there really are similarities. But I’m happy I reread this.<br /><br />I nearly forgot: this series tends to touch on big ideas in a way that makes the world feel bigger, and grounded, and also - weirdly influential? (<i>Were</i> these influential? I know they sold a lot, but I don’t think so.) And yet I can read stuff like this and wonder:<br /><blockquote>You’re aghast at the fact that I’ll bring an animal from Cloral or a weapon from Eelong, yet you are quick to bring something that is far more intrusive. You bring ideas, Pendragon! You were raised on Second Earth, and you are all too quick to impose what you feel are the higher morals of that territory on all others. How is that any different from what I have done?</blockquote>I read that and marveled, I really did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3129446310773406607" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_62159856" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62159856" />
    <a title="Jordan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2308874-jordan"><img alt="Jordan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421811649p2/2308874.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/62159856?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jordan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jordan" href="/user/show/2308874-jordan">Jordan</a>
      </span>

        rated it

    </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer62159856" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5991459353917929841">"...he may find out what it means to be a traveler.", says the back of the book. Does he...? I guess we'll find out. :P<br/><br/>Still... just... awesome. Awesomer, in fact. I think that this is my favorite book of the series yet. It totally must be. Because. I. Am. Officially. Insane. Seriously. Lol.<br/><br/>I love Quillan because I hate it. Which sounds contradictary, but it really isn't. I hate clowns, so what's cooler to me than a place where clowns are mentioned/run into often? It's a truly freaky place- beli</span>
  <span id="freeText5991459353917929841" style="display:none">"...he may find out what it means to be a traveler.", says the back of the book. Does he...? I guess we'll find out. :P<br /><br />Still... just... awesome. Awesomer, in fact. I think that this is my favorite book of the series yet. It totally must be. Because. I. Am. Officially. Insane. Seriously. Lol.<br /><br />I love Quillan because I hate it. Which sounds contradictary, but it really isn't. I hate clowns, so what's cooler to me than a place where clowns are mentioned/run into often? It's a truly freaky place- believe me. It gives me serious, and I mean SERIOUS, flash backs to 1984, not sure why. It also gave me flashbacks to the other Pendragon books, hehe.<br /><br />The story is getting more interesting. The stakes have again been upped. And so we go. The final twist is a major final twist. MAJOR. Oh, YES! And I thought I felt lonely reading it before. It's so weird... it's such a friendly, social type of book, and at the same time- It's very lonely. It occasionally shifts into this opressive feeling of loneliness. This book does more than the others. For obvious reasons that will be discovered upon reading. Just know that you will enter into a world of loneliness for Bobby. The final twist reminds me of... Well, I can't remember what the main one was, but it reminds me of several stories. Final Fantasy X, the Kingdom Hearts series, etc. No more of that though.<br /><br />The characters are still awesome. Mark and Courtney are all the better, as is Saint Dane. Have I mentioned how GREAT Saint Dane's personality is done? It's really, really well done. Saint Dane is like one of the top few best villains. Topped by only, like, Orpheaus because I hated the guy so much. Anyway, as far as the other travelers... Well, Remudi was ok, I guess. As was whats-her-name Nevva. Nevva reminded me of Cissnei from Final Fantasy 7:Crisis Core. She just... did. I pictured her looking like her sometimes, too. Notice that most of MacHale's girl characters are some odd twist on 'they think they can do everything and probably can do most'. Aja... Courtney... Loor... Kasha... all so different, but yet, such a similar concept. Nevva doesn't exactly break that pattern, but she's certainly different.<br /><br />And HA! I knew it. Bobby was getting pretty confident. I just KNEW it would- Wait, minor spoilers past here. Bobby's personality was pushed to be over confident. He was a bit out of personality, and at the end, it was explained WHY MacHale bothered pushing Bobby out of his personality. I forgive him though, the twist at the end was good enough to release my bitterness of Bobby saying "I knew I could win this thing."<br /><br />BTW... how will this all end? I've heard that the end is silly, but is the only thing that would've worked. This I heard from friends at the Youth Group :)<br /><br />Anyway, I have an active imagination in this area, and am having fun dreaming of the Travelers, lol I am so excited to read the eigth...<br /><br />HOBEY HO!!! Sorry, had to say that.<br /><br />And so we go. (haha)</span>

<div id="review_2408641331" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2408641331" />
    <a title="Deviki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2484174-deviki"><img alt="Deviki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311927680p2/2484174.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2408641331?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deviki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deviki" href="/user/show/2484174-deviki">Deviki</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2484174-deviki?shelf=diversity_mixed">diversity_mixed</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2408641331" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10075279193354512794">First off, I would like to apologize to myself and whoever is watching me read this series.....that I am so sorry i took too long to finish reading this book. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1508953171ra/24271017.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I did not do this on purpose, I had no choice...really!!. I have such a hectic month and I knew this book was impossible to read during that time. For a week I only managed to read 1 or 2 chapters while commuting to work and back. Thank god, this book is super intriguing and easy to get into....because reading this book in between all the </span>
  <span id="freeText10075279193354512794" style="display:none">First off, I would like to apologize to myself and whoever is watching me read this series.....that I am so sorry i took too long to finish reading this book. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1508953171ra/24271017.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I did not do this on purpose, I had no choice...really!!. I have such a hectic month and I knew this book was impossible to read during that time. For a week I only managed to read 1 or 2 chapters while commuting to work and back. Thank god, this book is super intriguing and easy to get into....because reading this book in between all the distraction was challenging ! <br><br>Alright alright enough whining .........<br><br>******MAJOR SPOILERS ALERT**********<br><br>After reading the final chapter............<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1529760794ra/25842607.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>WTH this book had so many twist and turns and hidden boogeman .........it was like running through a maze blindfolded!!!. Gosh this book is very different from the rest. No the concept is the same but for the first time ...........we have a different kind of traveler .......dayum......<br><br>Wow, even from the beginning of this book you know shit is about to get super real now. This book had taken a darker turn ......but not just for Bobby but for Courtney and Mark too. Especially to the latter. Gosh this book is super jammed packed. Maybe I feel like this book is super long but maybe its because I took that long to read LOL. <br><br>There is something significantly different about this book. Bobby's new territory adventure is a lil bit different. He gets into trouble and learn about this new territory the hard way. Although not so bad compare to Eelong. The difference here is that Bobby is better prepared. When he gets into trouble its not like he is gonna get his arse kicked like in the previous adventure. <br><br>I like this new and confident Bobby, I think his training in Zadaa really helped him a lot. It sure prepared him for what he is about to face. Bobby is amazingly strong. Even when we first get introduced by Nevva, I wasn't sure I liked her all that much. One is because she didn't seem to show much concern about another traveler dying. I mean she did show some emotion but she was quick to brush it aside. Not to mention, she set him up as a challenger even without considering if he is ready or capable. Hearing stories is not enough. There was something fishy about her........<br><br>This territory is messed up like all hope is lost messed up. I hate to say this but this book reminded me of Hunger Games but looking at the publishing year ......It looks like D.J Machale was first to publish this book in 2006, while Hunger Games came out in 2008. Anyway, this territory is a gambling and slaving by all mighty super mega store LOL. When you put it like that ....it is funny !!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1483474066ra/21616225.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So we learn about the workings and disasters of this territory from Bobby finding things out the wrong way. I really pity Bobby, he is always subject to brutal reality when he jumps into new territory. In this case, he was put to the test the moment he came through the flume. <br><br>I didn't particularly like the games in this book. I mean sure it was interesting and creative. But compare to the "The Reality Bug" book, this one didn't quite capture my interest. Maybe a lot of the games reminded me of "Takashi castle game show". To me this book kind of lacked the creativity the Reality Bug had. However, that did not make the book any less interesting because everything else besides the game is hella mind blowing. <br><br>Quillan is a perfect example of how our own world or country can turn out if there is only one single power for all. So the time Bobby arrive this world is a dystopian of its own worse mistakes. This world has been like that for long long time. So the old world cultures and lifestyle is now an unsure myth. I'm not sure sure I buy the fact that this world became like this because the people wanted cheaper things ...........I mean sure everyone loves a bargain but how can a stupendous wealthy people be ok buying the same thing as the average people. How can everyone be ok with buying bland things. Humans love a good bargain but we also like to keep things appealing, we are indecisive people who always crave something new and original. How could everyone be ok with going back to something deprived and disenchanting of culture and newer lifestyle. That is one thing that didn't sit right for me in this book. <br><br>Who saw through Green challenger ? I did !!! You know why ? Because Saint Dane was trying a lil too hard to get Bobby to play. He "literally" had him sent an invitation to join the Grand X in a silver plate. And you know already that he loves kicking Bobby around for fun. So why not be one of the challenger right ? I also didn't see the plot twist with Veego and LaBerge. I thought the game was familiar because of Saint Dane's influence as a trustee. Gosh it seem like the flume had become a commercial all can fly budget plane. <br><br>I really felt bad for Bobby ......even after he won the game and had his glory moments. The territory still fell back to its old devastating ways. I knew there was something fishy about Nevva, but I honestly didn't think she would join force with him. I thought she wanted power like the trustees not join that jerk. The fact she caused the death of another Traveler is already bad enough!!!. I knew the old lady would be important to the story later, because she was mentioned in a strange way and alluring way. <br><br>How the story turned out back in Second Earth was even more shocking, especially what happened to Mark. Gosh honestly everything was going fine (yes I know about Andy) but for Saint McDick to go that low to get his evil plans working is flabbergasting. Courtney left Mark to deal with acolyte thing for awhile but now it is her turn. I feel bad for her, because she is not fully recovered and Mark is nowhere in sane mind to help her. Thank god, Bobby arrived when he did. I wonder what happened to him. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1485278901ra/21800306.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I didn't even see the last plot twist in the book. Gosh! does that mean Mark will be "helping" Saint McDick along with his evil plan? Because it looks like his technology creation is beyond what he is capable of. Nevva lost her parents and that drove her to join Saint Dane, did the same thing happened to Mark ? I don't believe it !! Mark is a deep thinker, he is very careful and meticulous about his knowledge of Saint Dane and Halla. I don't think he willingly joined Saint Dane. <br><br>On the side note, Saint Dane is extremely patient dude. I mean Courtney, Mark and Bobby knew him from pre school ...........and they are 17 years old now. That's a long term plan he had for Bobby. Not to mention his plans for other territory. Because whenever Bobby jumps into a new territory, Saint Dane's influence and planning is playing out for long time. Dude is hella busy man!! You need a new hobby dude !!<br><br>Sometimes Saint Dane confuse me, what execetly does he want with Bobby. He don't seem very concern with other Traveler much. But he seem to have personal vendetta against Bobby. I think even his dealings with Uncle Press is because of Bobby. Why is Bobby so important to him ? He wants he to be strong, he wants him to fight and he wants him to find out about himself. Why ? <br>So we finally have 2% answer to who Saint Dane is working or answers to or the ultimate goal ? The Convergence ............I'm so bloody confused!!<br><br>I can't wait to find out more ...........there is only 3 more books left ........I can't wait!!! <br><br>Omg, did I ever mention this before? I love how Bobby is aging in every book cover. Like we get to watch him grown up :) He looks really handsome in this cover :P<br>Even though this book don't have Loor in person, she is mentioned in almost every other chapter.....hehehe I likey ........</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17177332221158490128">Another installment in the Pendragon series. This one is disheartening--but I think it is intended to be. I wouldn't recommend this book on its own--but as part of the series--you have to read it. The plot of Quillan isn't compelling--but the discoveries made in the broader story arch make the book worth the read.</span>

<div id="review_2925053646" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4500645355733349071">Better than the others. Enjoyed the twist. </span>

<div id="review_176177473" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/176177473" />
    <a title="Aparajitabasu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4790652-aparajitabasu"><img alt="Aparajitabasu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311701802p2/4790652.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/176177473?book_show_action=true">Jun 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aparajitabasu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aparajitabasu" href="/user/show/4790652-aparajitabasu">Aparajitabasu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4790652-aparajitabasu?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4790652-aparajitabasu?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4790652-aparajitabasu?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4790652-aparajitabasu?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4790652-aparajitabasu?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4790652-aparajitabasu?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer176177473" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer736713385390045330">Moving onto the next journal in the <i>
  <b>Pendragron</b>
</i> saga is book <i>
  <b>#7 The Quillan Games</b>
</i>. And the plot gets messed up.<br/><br/><br/>Here is the summary:<br/><br/><br/><i>Each new episode seems to raise the stakes of this action adventure series. In the seventh installment, Bobby Pendragon realizes that the Quillan Territory can be saved only by defeating game masters Veego and LaBerge in a fateful competition: Winning the Quillan Games could bring him a giant step closer to understanding the meaning of being a Traveler. Losing</i></span>
  <span id="freeText736713385390045330" style="display:none">Moving onto the next journal in the <i>
  <b>Pendragron</b>
</i> saga is book <i>
  <b>#7 The Quillan Games</b>
</i>. And the plot gets messed up.<br /><br /><br />Here is the summary:<br /><br /><br /><i>Each new episode seems to raise the stakes of this action adventure series. In the seventh installment, Bobby Pendragon realizes that the Quillan Territory can be saved only by defeating game masters Veego and LaBerge in a fateful competition: Winning the Quillan Games could bring him a giant step closer to understanding the meaning of being a Traveler. Losing brings instant extinction.</i><br /><br />In this one, Bobby Pendragon, the young hero of the series,travels to the territory of Quillan, a dark world with no emotion and is controlled by a company called BLOK. Bobby soon learns what the turning-point of this world may be, since he finds out that everyone on Quillan gambles on a series of sports and games called The Quillan Games. However the people of Quillan don't bet on the games with money....but with their own lives, and if they lose, they'll pay. Determined to stop the territory from colliding, Bobby ends up becoming one of the champions, under the control of two spectators named Veego and LaBarge, and competes in a series of deadly games and tasks, risking his life for the sake of all of Quillan and, even greater, all of Halla. <br /><br />While Bobby is dealing with the insanity on Quillan, Mark and Courtney are trying to put their lives back together on Second Earth. Courtney is still recovering from her "accident" at the end of the sixth book, and Mark is spending a lot of time with Andy Mitchell, his ex-worst enemy. I don't want to say much more about the plot, other than, Saint Dane promises Bobby to reveal the "true nature" of the Travelers if he does......something for him. Like all the Pendragon books, the story is action-packed and very exciting. However, the book never becomes formulaic because of some unusual plot twists, and interesting, if slightly creepy, character development. The series has gotten much darker since the first book, but still has its funny moments. <br /><br />The first 200 pages really dragged. I have never noticed that the author spent so much time describing every detail for us. Maybe it was excessive in this book. I thought at first it was maybe that there is so much backtracking in his books (why does he think that every book is being read by someone who has not read any of the other books of this series?) but it wasn't the backtracking. It was the endless descriptions of uninteresting aspects of Quillan. Saint Dane doesn't even begin to appear until mid-way through the book. Up till that point, I really didn't care what happened on Quillan. From then on, "Quillan" begins to shine as the other books have done so before it. The battle of wills between Boddy and Saint Dane really are the high points of the novels: will Bobby let himself be drawn in? Will Saint Dane gain a point against him? What is the plan for this territory? <br /><br />Now I can't say much because this series is actually meant for the adolescent age-group and not for me and doesn't even appeal to me but my complain - the lack of background information - the major flaw this series suffers from - Mr. Machale, don't you think that by the 7th book it is time to start resolving some of the conflicts your previous books have introduced? Well, I do. And I can't help but think that a lot of other fans out there feel the same way, even though the reviews here are overly glowing. I'll admit that the book is action packed. This is no doubt responsible for the great reviews, especially from your biggest audience the adolescent. Still, at some point even the youngest fan is going to want to know the answers to their questions about travelers. How are they selected? Where are they really from? What happens to their parents? What does it really mean to be a traveler? This book promised to provide some of those long awaited for answers. What it gave is one statement from Saint Dane that travelers are an illusion. Gee, no kidding! I think we understood that about six books ago.<br /><br />All of McHale's books have basically the same storyline with Saint Daine, the monstrous Travelor determined on destroying Bobby, appearing and attempting to destroy a Territory. Each and every time Bobby manages to foil him. Tip for the writer.. it's getting a little boring. The only inspiration I have to keep reading this series is the desire to find out how Bobby manages to survive this time. I don't know how McHale is going to keep up the suspense for another maybe 3 books. Let's wait an see shall we?</span>
  <a data-text-id="736713385390045330" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1924441550" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1924441550" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2682082-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595974239p2/2682082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1924441550?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/2682082-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2682082-amanda?shelf=adventure-thriller">adventure-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2682082-amanda?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1924441550" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14825487214336378044"><i>"There are two types of people in this world. People who hate clowns...and clowns."</i><br/><br/>^ I identify very strongly with this quote.<br/><br/>Also, let's just get it out of the way right now that I've been pronouncing the title of this book "The Killin Games" and it's given me a lot more giggles than it probably should.<br/><br/>This is the 7th book in D.J. Machale's Pendragon series, which revolves around Bobby Pendragon, the Traveler from Second Earth (there are three Earths cause we're just the most important territor</span>
  <span id="freeText14825487214336378044" style="display:none"><i>"There are two types of people in this world. People who hate clowns...and clowns."</i><br /><br />^ I identify very strongly with this quote.<br /><br />Also, let's just get it out of the way right now that I've been pronouncing the title of this book "The Killin Games" and it's given me a lot more giggles than it probably should.<br /><br />This is the 7th book in D.J. Machale's Pendragon series, which revolves around Bobby Pendragon, the Traveler from Second Earth (there are three Earths cause we're just the most important territory obviously). Bobby has spent the last three years or so traveling through the ten territories of Halla, which comprise all of time and space. The big bad in this series is Saint Dane, a demon traveler who wants to bring all of Halla into chaos so he can rule over it himself. But don't worry, he's doing it all for the best.<br /><br />I remember beginning this series when I was around 13 - we were on a vacation to Disneyworld and all I really wanted to do was sit on the patio and read The Merchant of Death. What a dork. Now, 10 years later, on a beautiful weekend, all I wanted to do was finish The Quillan Games (heh. Killin). What's really obvious to me, reading this after The Hunger Games was published, is the striking similarities between the two. This book was published in 2006, while The Hunger Games came out in 2008, but it's a bit uncanny how many ties there are between the two.<br /><br />On this territory, Quillan, a huge corporation owns pretty much everything and everyone, and forces people to compete in games in order to survive or have enough food to eat. The games are publicized, and the only source of entertainment for the people. Of course, their darker purpose is to keep the people under control and distracted. Bobby is a challenger in the games, and rebels from the territory want him to be a symbol of hope for the rebellion, even calling him "a tribute" to the people of Quillan. "We want a symbol. A spark. It doesn't have to be huge, but it must be stirring." So, yeah. D.J. Machale did it first, y'all.<br /><br />I found this installation in the Pendragon series pretty thrilling and intriguing, but I do think a good 100 pages could have been cut out, and none would have been worse for the wear. The books are all written in the form of a journal from Bobby to his friends back home on Second Earth, which means lots of recap and introspection opportunities, and the author makes heavy usage of these. MacHale does great with the action scenes, but his writing tends to be a bit choppy, i.e. "At least I thought it was a wall. It sure felt like one. It was hard. It was flat. It stretched out on either side of me. You know... wall." When the action is going, you don't notice the choppiness as much, but it's really evident with the amount of downtime in this book.<br /><br />Saint Dane is always a great villain, and I think it's because of his persuasive powers. He really has a way of making Bobby and the other travelers question their purpose and what the "right thing" is to do. He reminds me of an intellectual, but evil genius - the things he says make complete sense, but when you actually look a little deeper, it's just fancy words on top of violence and greed. There's a pretty big betrayal in this book on account of Saint Dane's power to manipulate.<br /><br />I do wish that there had been more secrets revealed about the nature of the travelers themselves in this book. It was hinted and teased at, but no new information really appeared, which is a shame. I've been wanting to know what happened with Bobby's family since the first book, but we're still no closer to discovering the dealio. This book does a great job at setting up for the next one though, and there are some great storylines I can see forming up ahead. I may have started this series 10 years ago, but I won't be taking that long to finish them. They're thrilling, action-packed, and are finally beginning to mature enough to where I don't feel embarrassed reading them in the privacy of my home.<br /><br />If you'd like to hear more of my babblings, please visit my blog, <a href="https://thebookslothblog.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book Sloth</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14825487214336378044" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer853255909" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9903253321663579399">First read: May, 2007<br/>Re-read: July 22, 2014<br/><br/>Although this is technically a fantasy novel, the world of Quillan definitely has a dystopian feel. I absolutely love dytopians, but the one thing that I typically complain about is that the world wasn't developed enough. I love learning all about the worlds that dystopians are set in. What most people call an "info dump" I think of as a really interesting learning section. Fortunately, what DJ MacHale does best is world-building. And this world is incr</span>
  <span id="freeText9903253321663579399" style="display:none">First read: May, 2007<br />Re-read: July 22, 2014<br /><br />Although this is technically a fantasy novel, the world of Quillan definitely has a dystopian feel. I absolutely love dytopians, but the one thing that I typically complain about is that the world wasn't developed enough. I love learning all about the worlds that dystopians are set in. What most people call an "info dump" I think of as a really interesting learning section. Fortunately, what DJ MacHale does best is world-building. And this world is incredibly interesting and well-developed. It's one of my favorite territories in the series. And the plot is really exciting too. I love seeing all of the different challenges and competitors. Going into this book the 2nd time, I considered it to be my favorite in the series. It's fallen a couple slots, but that's mostly because there were a couple books that I ended up liking more than I remembered the first time. Overall, I really like the plot and the world.<br /><br />9/10 (4.5/5)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9903253321663579399" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2858703724949629242">This is the 7th book in a 9 book series about a kid who is chosen to become a hero between worlds. The main character, Bobby Pendragon is someone who is traveling through space and time in order to stop the antagonist, Saint Dane from bringing chaos to all the worlds. In the Quillan Games, Pendragon travels to a world called Quillan in order to stop Saint Dane. <br/><br/>Throughout the whole series, which I enjoy a great deal, MacHale keeps all the characters dynamic and brings new surprises with every bo</span>
  <span id="freeText2858703724949629242" style="display:none">This is the 7th book in a 9 book series about a kid who is chosen to become a hero between worlds. The main character, Bobby Pendragon is someone who is traveling through space and time in order to stop the antagonist, Saint Dane from bringing chaos to all the worlds. In the Quillan Games, Pendragon travels to a world called Quillan in order to stop Saint Dane. <br /><br />Throughout the whole series, which I enjoy a great deal, MacHale keeps all the characters dynamic and brings new surprises with every book. As this book is nearing the end, the climax is reaching a critical point, making this book important to the story. <br /><br />I recommend the entire series, as it is a great and original story. </span>

<div id="review_2024289985" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2024289985" />
    <a title="Nina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20966982-nina"><img alt="Nina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496991380p2/20966982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2024289985?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nina" href="/user/show/20966982-nina">Nina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" " href="/book/show/13500863-the-quillan-games">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2024289985" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15740440037082519593">TLDR: If you thought the previous book was rough and tedious, keep reading, because starting this book, you won't regret it.<br/><br/>---------<br/><br/>I'm still not sure how I felt about this book. It started out excruciatingly slow, with mindless action that seemed to span several chapters (and felt like almost a fifth through the book) before Pendragon gets anywhere near finding out anything about the territory. Once he was finally captured by Blok and was made to compete in the games, the book had my attention</span>
  <span id="freeText15740440037082519593" style="display:none">TLDR: If you thought the previous book was rough and tedious, keep reading, because starting this book, you won't regret it.<br /><br />---------<br /><br />I'm still not sure how I felt about this book. It started out excruciatingly slow, with mindless action that seemed to span several chapters (and felt like almost a fifth through the book) before Pendragon gets anywhere near finding out anything about the territory. Once he was finally captured by Blok and was made to compete in the games, the book had my attention. It was good. Very. The games were death interesting, sure, but I'm not talking about that. What was good was learning more about Nevva Winter (the Traveler of Quillan), and learning more about Blok and this messed up territory that seems set to doom from the get-go. The story takes a much darker tone in this one. Bobby's matured, and not just Bobby; Courtney's all fired up and recovering from her injuries in the previous book, and boy, is she ready to rip Saint Dane a new one; and Mark goes through an odd friendship with an unlikely individual (Andy Mitchell) that makes you want to scream because all your warning flags are up thanks to the ending of the previous book. The story is officially no longer about just Bobby. Courtney and Mark are no longer bystanders. They're part of the game, and their roles are starting. And it's great. You can feel it building up to something. I get excited when the story segments back to Second Earth. <br /><br />And with the characters growing up, so does the plot, the depth of Saint Dane, and the themes in the book. The revolution of this territory, the subject of hope (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and how it easily crumbles <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>) all take a much darker and more serious tone compared to the previous books. And that ending! The ending makes you want to dive into the next one, like, yes! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Like, holyshit, Nevva's betrayal was mind-boggling and I loved every second of it. And Mark! What happened to Mark? Also, Veego and LaBerge being from Veelox? Like, woaaaaah! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> DUN DUN DUNNNNNN<br /><br />Diving into the next book.<br />Hobey ho, let's go!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15740440037082519593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maberan Potato" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maberan Potato" href="/user/show/47565421-maberan-potato">Maberan Potato</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781416934493" href="/book/show/7145910-the-quillan-games">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47565421-maberan-potato?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47565421-maberan-potato?shelf=read-in-english">read-in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47565421-maberan-potato?shelf=bronze">bronze</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47565421-maberan-potato?shelf=both-pov">both-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47565421-maberan-potato?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47565421-maberan-potato?shelf=alternate-world-fantasy">alternate-world-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47565421-maberan-potato?shelf=four-stars">four-stars</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2127630780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14028563718662678414">YES THIS IS WHAT I'M TALKING ABOUT!!! It took a while, but I can finally say that this series deserved my love as a child and it is thus perfect and untouchable.<br/><br/>Seriously tho this series is getting serious! I like how it's not always the same thing either? As the characters age, the rules change and Saint Dane is getting some more depth. It's not always 'must stop X from doing Z' is what I mean. Sometimes SD' plot involve external stuff, and sometimes even Bobby is the trigger. It's different.<br/><br/>Bu</span>
  <span id="freeText14028563718662678414" style="display:none">YES THIS IS WHAT I'M TALKING ABOUT!!! It took a while, but I can finally say that this series deserved my love as a child and it is thus perfect and untouchable.<br /><br />Seriously tho this series is getting serious! I like how it's not always the same thing either? As the characters age, the rules change and Saint Dane is getting some more depth. It's not always 'must stop X from doing Z' is what I mean. Sometimes SD' plot involve external stuff, and sometimes even Bobby is the trigger. It's different.<br /><br />But I liked this book more than most. Stuff's happening in both Bobby's journals and the real world so it's great! Bobby's really becoming a smart-ass too which is the best thing ever. Saint Dane is evolving, the Travelers are evolving, SHIT'S GETTING REAL BRO.<br /><br />The plot's pacing is okay, there's definitely room for amelioration but what can you do. The characters were fun, especially Bobby. The world of Quillian was different and the games were cool, and I like that it happens after Bobby trained as a warrior because he TOTALLY WOULD'VE DIED IF HE'D DONE THIS BEFORE ZADAA. It gives a good reason why he's so badass.<br /><br />BUT I believe the end was just nonsensical??? Like, sure, it HURTS when just as your hope is at its peak, it gets crushed to bits, but these people have nothing to lose now! If I'd been there, I'd have jumped on some wall or something and yelled "WE CAN MAKE OUR OWN!! FUCK THESE BITCHES!!!" and graffitied on the wall or something. Like revolutions do not get crushed like that. Anger would've made these people even more violent and determinate.<br /><br />But yes this was fun. SHIT'S GETTING REAL have I said it enough yet do you get it hahaha</span>
  <a data-text-id="14028563718662678414" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ao6F3qjAYHlowaDnKpYzgNYzYxnFTA4oFNS/bCou/5pqa6XeDsyUJj28W2mOqwlQm4fO+GLYLaiHThRsuyc5aQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('X3e8eYq2LavVFd14gRPDCotrHMcy3tdYN66nEhGpyblfkpx5LLrZ9IBoJvYlLvnaxt+xJpVK9NikNAwSgKAPSg==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/74046.D_J_MacHale">About D.J. MacHale</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/74046.D_J_MacHale"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1418514923p3/74046.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/74046.D_J_MacHale">D.J. MacHale

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer18440337065218781881">D.J. MacHale is a writer, director, executive producer and creator of several popular television series and movies.<br/><br/>He was raised in Greenwich, CT and graduated from Greenwich High School. While in school, he had several jobs including collecting eggs at a poultry farm, engraving sports trophies and washing dishes in a steakhouse...in between playing football and running track. D.J. then attended N</span>
  <span id="freeText18440337065218781881" style="display:none">D.J. MacHale is a writer, director, executive producer and creator of several popular television series and movies.<br /><br />He was raised in Greenwich, CT and graduated from Greenwich High School. While in school, he had several jobs including collecting eggs at a poultry farm, engraving sports trophies and washing dishes in a steakhouse...in between playing football and running track. D.J. then attended New York University where he received a BFA in film production.<br /><br />His filmmaking career began in New York where he worked as a freelance writer/director, making corporate videos and television commercials. He also taught photography and film production.<br /><br />D.J. broke into the entertainment business by writing several ABC Afterschool Specials. After moving to Los Angeles, he made the fulltime switch from informational films, to entertainment. As co-creator of the popular Nickelodeon series: Are You Afraid of the Dark?, he produced all 91 episodes over 8 years. He wrote and directed many of the episodes including the CableAce nominated The Tale of Cutter's Treasure starring Charles S. Dutton. He was nominated for a Gemini award for directing The Tale of the Dangerous Soup starring Neve Campbell.<br /><br />D.J. also wrote and directed the movie Tower of Terror for ABC's Wonderful World of Disney which starred Kirsten Dunst and Steve Guttenberg. The Showtime series Chris Cross was co-created, written and produced by D.J. It received the CableAce award for Best Youth Series.<br /><br />D.J. co-created and produced the Discovery Kids series Flight 29 Down for which he writes all the episodes and directs several. His work on Flight 29 Down has earned him both Writers Guild of America and Directors Guild of America award nominations.<br /><br />Other notable writing credits include the classic ABC Afterschool Special titled Seasonal Differences; the pilot for the long-running PBS/CBS series Ghostwriter; and the HBO series Encyclopedia Brown, Boy Detective for which he received a CableAce nomination for writing.<br /><br />In print, D.J. has co-written the book The Tale of the Nightly Neighbors, based on his own teleplay and penned the poetic adaptation of the classic Norwegian folk tale East of the Sun and West of the Moon.<br /><br />The book series: Pendragon - Journal of an Adventure through Time and Space marks D.J.'s first turn as a novelist. He plans for this series of Young Adult adventures to span a total of 10 books.<br /><br />D.J. lives in Southern California with his wife Evangeline and daughter Keaton. They are avid backpackers, scuba divers and skiers. Rounding out the household are a Golden Retriever, Maggie; and a Kitten, Kaboodle. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18440337065218781881" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
